# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

Perfect! I've successfully created a comprehensive analysis of how `/healthz` and `/readyz` endpoints are implemented across the three repositories. Here's what I found:

## Summary

**Answer file created:** `/workspace/answer.json`

### Key Findings:

**Kubernetes** uses a sophisticated **pluggable health checker framework**:
- Endpoints: `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`
- Implements a `HealthChecker` interface with named checkers (PingHealthz, LogHealthz, InformerSyncHealthz, ShutdownHealthz)
- Supports grace periods for liveness checks
- Includes rich checks for dependencies (informers, etcd, KMS)

**Grafana** uses a **state-based approach with database checks**:
- Endpoints: `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`, `/api/health`
- Uses `HealthNotifier` for thread-safe readiness signaling
- `/api/health` endpoint checks database connectivity and returns JSON with database status and version info
- Simpler middleware-based registration

**Prometheus** uses **state-based readiness with graceful shutdown tracking**:
- Endpoints: `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready`
- Three-state system: Ready, NotReady, Stopping
- `testReady()` middleware wraps handlers to enforce readiness checks
- Includes `X-Prometheus-Stopping` header to indicate graceful shutdown state
- Both endpoints support GET and HEAD methods

The analysis includes complete file paths, relevant symbols, call chains, and a detailed comparison table showing the architectural differences between the three approaches.

management\\n\\n**Key Components**:\\n- **HealthChecker Interface**: Named health checkers that perform individual checks. Built-in checkers include:\\n  - `PingHealthz`: Always returns healthy\\n  - `LogHealthz`: Checks if logging is not blocked\\n  - `InformerSyncHealthz`: Checks if informers are synced (used for readyz)\\n  - `ShutdownHealthz`: Fails when shutdown signal is received\\n  - Custom named checks via `NamedCheck()` and `NamedGroupedCheck()`\\n\\n- **Registration Pattern**: `InstallHandler()`, `InstallReadyzHandler()`, and `InstallLivezHandler()` functions register health endpoints on a mux with a list of HealthChecker instances\\n\\n- **Checks Performed**:\\n  - `/healthz`: Backward compatibility endpoint, includes ping and custom checks\\n  - `/livez` (liveness): Checks if the process is alive (with configurable grace period via `livezGracePeriod`)\\n  - `/readyz` (readiness): Strict checks ensuring the server can handle traffic (informer sync, etcd access, KMS health, etc.)\\n\\n- **Graceful Shutdown**: `AddBootSequenceHealthChecks()` and `AddReadyzShutdownCheck()` allow configuring shutdown behavior\\n\\n### Grafana/Grafana\\n\\n**Endpoints**: `/healthz`, `/livez`, `/readyz`, `/api/health`\\n\\n**Implementation Files**:\\n- `pkg/server/health.go`: Core health endpoint handlers (`LivezHandler`, `ReadyzHandler`)\\n- `pkg/api/http_server.go`: HTTP server integration and health check middleware registration\\n\\n**Key Components**:\\n- **HealthNotifier**: Thread-safe mechanism to signal readiness state using atomic bool\\n  - `SetReady()`: Mark operator as ready\\n  - `SetNotReady()`: Mark operator as not ready\\n  - `IsReady()`: Check readiness status\\n\\n- **Handler Implementations**:\\n  - `LivezHandler()`: Always returns 200 OK (process is alive)\\n  - `ReadyzHandler(HealthNotifier)`: Returns 200 OK if ready, 503 Service Unavailable if not ready\\n  - `healthzHandler()`: Simple middleware-based check, returns 200 OK if server is running\\n  - `apiHealthHandler()`: Checks database connectivity, returns 200 if database is OK, 503 if failing. Includes version info in response\\n\\n- **Checks Performed**:\\n  - `/healthz`: Basic server running check (always 200)\\n  - `/readyz`: Operator readiness state (depends on `HealthNotifier.SetReady()` being called)\\n  - `/livez`: Process liveness (always 200)\\n  - `/api/health`: Database connectivity check, returns JSON with database status and version information\\n\\n- **Registration**: Handlers are registered as middleware using `m.Use(handler)` in the HTTP server setup\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus\\n\\n**Endpoints**: `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready`\\n\\n**Implementation Files**:\\n- `web/web.go`: Main handler registration and readiness checking logic\\n- `cmd/prometheus/main.go`: Server initialization and readiness state management\\n\\n**Key Components**:\\n- **Handler**: Main web handler managing the application's ready state\\n  - `SetReady(status ReadyStatus)`: Sets the ready status (Ready, NotReady, or Stopping)\\n  - `isReady()`: Checks current ready status\\n  - `testReady(f http.HandlerFunc)`: Middleware that wraps handlers to enforce ready status checks\\n\\n- **ReadyStatus Enum**: Three states:\\n  - `Ready`: Server is operational and accepting traffic\\n  - `NotReady`: Server is initializing but may become ready\\n  - `Stopping`: Server is shutting down gracefully\\n\\n- **Handler Implementations**:\\n  - `/-/healthy`: Always returns 200 OK (\\\"<AppName> is Healthy.\\\")\\n  - `/-/ready`: Wraps response with `testReady()` middleware\\n    - Returns 200 OK when in Ready state\\n    - Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: false` header when NotReady\\n    - Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true` header when Stopping\\n  - Both endpoints support GET and HEAD methods\\n\\n- **Checks Performed**:\\n  - `/-/healthy`: Always succeeds (simple liveness indicator)\\n  - `/-/ready`: Checks internal ready state managed by `SetReady()` during server initialization and shutdown. Ready status is set after TSDB initialization completes and unset during graceful shutdown.\\n\\n### Comparison Summary\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Grafana | Prometheus |\\n|--------|-----------|---------|------------|\\n| **Architecture** | Pluggable health checker framework | State-based readiness with database check | State-based with graceful shutdown tracking |\\n| **Liveness** | `/livez` with grace period | `/livez` (always 200) | `/-/healthy` (always 200) |\\n| **Readiness** | `/readyz` with rich checks | `/readyz` (state-based) | `/-/ready` (state-based) |\\n| **Dependencies Checked** | Informers, etcd, KMS, custom | Database connectivity | Internal initialization state |\\n| **Shutdown Support** | Explicit shutdown health check | (via HealthNotifier) | Dedicated Stopping state with header |\\n| **Response Format** | Text (\\\"ok\\\" or error list) | Text/JSON (database status, version) | Text (status message) |\\n| **Extensibility** | Add custom HealthChecker instances | Extend via HealthNotifier signals | Modify SetReady() calls in main |\\n\"\n}\n",

Includes version info in response\\n\\n- **Checks Performed**:\\n  - `/healthz`: Basic server running check (always 200)\\n  - `/readyz`: Operator readiness state (depends on `HealthNotifier.SetReady()` being called)\\n  - `/livez`: Process liveness (always 200)\\n  - `/api/health`: Database connectivity check, returns JSON with database status and version information\\n\\n- **Registration**: Handlers are registered as middleware using `m.Use(handler)` in the HTTP server setup\\n\\n### Prometheus/Prometheus\\n\\n**Endpoints**: `/-/healthy`, `/-/ready`\\n\\n**Implementation Files**:\\n- `web/web.go`: Main handler registration and readiness checking logic\\n- `cmd/prometheus/main.go`: Server initialization and readiness state management\\n\\n**Key Components**:\\n- **Handler**: Main web handler managing the application's ready state\\n  - `SetReady(status ReadyStatus)`: Sets the ready status (Ready, NotReady, or Stopping)\\n  - `isReady()`: Checks current ready status\\n  - `testReady(f http.HandlerFunc)`: Middleware that wraps handlers to enforce ready status checks\\n\\n- **ReadyStatus Enum**: Three states:\\n  - `Ready`: Server is operational and accepting traffic\\n  - `NotReady`: Server is initializing but may become ready\\n  - `Stopping`: Server is shutting down gracefully\\n\\n- **Handler Implementations**:\\n  - `/-/healthy`: Always returns 200 OK (\\\"<AppName> is Healthy.\\\")\\n  - `/-/ready`: Wraps response with `testReady()` middleware\\n    - Returns 200 OK when in Ready state\\n    - Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: false` header when NotReady\\n    - Returns 503 Service Unavailable with `X-Prometheus-Stopping: true` header when Stopping\\n  - Both endpoints support GET and HEAD methods\\n\\n- **Checks Performed**:\\n  - `/-/healthy`: Always succeeds (simple liveness indicator)\\n  - `/-/ready`: Checks internal ready state managed by `SetReady()` during server initialization and shutdown. Ready status is set after TSDB initialization completes and unset during graceful shutdown.\\n\\n### Comparison Summary\\n\\n| Aspect | Kubernetes | Grafana | Prometheus |\\n|--------|-----------|---------|------------|\\n| **Architecture** | Pluggable health checker framework | State-based readiness with database check | State-based with graceful shutdown tracking |\\n| **Liveness** | `/livez` with grace period | `/livez` (always 200) | `/-/healthy` (always 200) |\\n| **Readiness** | `/readyz` with rich checks | `/readyz` (state-based) | `/-/ready` (state-based) |\\n| **Dependencies Checked** | Informers, etcd, KMS, custom | Database connectivity | Internal initialization state |\\n| **Shutdown Support** | Explicit shutdown health check | (via HealthNotifier) | Dedicated Stopping state with header |\\n| **Response Format** | Text (\\\"ok\\\" or error list) | Text/JSON (database status, version) | Text (status message) |\\n| **Extensibility** | Add custom HealthChecker instances | Extend via HealthNotifier signals | Modify SetReady() calls in main |\\n\"\n}\n",
